>>>REPORT

# Qwen3 Small Models Research Report (as of Feb 16, 2026)

## 1. Models Overview

### Qwen3-1.7B
- **Type:** Dense Causal Language Model
- **Total Parameters:** 1.7B (1.4B non-embedding)
- **Architecture:** 28 layers, 16 Q heads / 8 KV heads (GQA), SwiGLU, RoPE, RMSNorm, QK-Norm
- **Context Length:** 32,768 tokens (32K native, with YARN/DCA can extend to ~128K inference)
- **Training Data:** ~36 trillion tokens, 119 languages
- **License:** Apache 2.0
- **Key Feature:** Hybrid thinking/non-thinking mode â can do step-by-step reasoning OR fast direct answers, switchable via `/think` and `/no_think`

### Qwen3-0.6B
- **Type:** Dense Causal Language Model
- **Total Parameters:** 0.6B (0.44B non-embedding)
- **Architecture:** 28 layers, 16 Q heads / 8 KV heads (GQA), same arch as 1.7B
- **Context Length:** 32,768 tokens
- **License:** Apache 2.0

---

## 2. Benchmarks (Base Models, from Qwen3 Technical Report arXiv:2505.09388, Table 8)

| Benchmark | Qwen2.5-0.5B-Base | **Qwen3-0.6B-Base** | Gemma-3-1B-Base | Qwen2.5-1.5B-Base | **Qwen3-1.7B-Base** |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **MMLU** (5-shot) | 47.50 | 52.81 | 26.26 | 60.90 | **62.63** |
| **MMLU-Pro** (5-shot, CoT) | 15.69 | 24.74 | 9.72 | 28.53 | **36.76** |
| **BBH** (3-shot, CoT) | 20.30 | 41.47 | 28.13 | 45.10 | **54.47** |
| **SuperGPQA** | 11.30 | 15.03 | 7.19 | 17.64 | **20.92** |
| **GPQA** | 24.75 | 26.77 | 24.75 | 24.24 | **28.28** |
| **GSM8K** (math) | 41.62 | 59.59 | 2.20 | 68.54 | **75.44** |
| **MATH** | 19.48 | 32.44 | 3.66 | 35.00 | **43.50** |
| **EvalPlus** (coding avg) | 31.85 | 36.23 | 8.98 | 44.80 | **52.70** |
| **MultiPL-E** (multi-lang code) | 18.70 | 24.58 | 5.15 | 33.10 | **42.71** |
| **MBPP** (3-shot) | 29.80 | 36.60 | 9.20 | 43.60 | **55.40** |
| **CRUX-O** (code reasoning) | 12.10 | 27.00 | 3.80 | 29.60 | **36.40** |
| **MGSM** (multilingual math) | 12.07 | 30.99 | 1.74 | 32.82 | **50.71** |
| **MMMLU** (multilingual) | 31.53 | 50.16 | 26.57 | 60.27 | **63.27** |

**Key takeaway from Qwen team:** "Qwen3-1.7B-Base outperforms Qwen2.5-3B-Base on over half of benchmarks, especially on STEM-related and coding benchmarks."

---

## 3. Coding Performance Analysis

### Qwen3-1.7B-Base vs Qwen2.5-1.5B-Base (coding):
- **EvalPlus:** 52.70 vs 44.80 (+17.6% improvement)
- **MultiPL-E:** 42.71 vs 33.10 (+29% improvement)
- **MBPP:** 55.40 vs 43.60 (+27% improvement)
- **CRUX-O:** 36.40 vs 29.60 (+23% improvement)

### Qwen3-1.7B vs Qwen2.5-Coder-1.5B Comparison:
- **Qwen2.5-Coder-1.5B-Instruct** is a **code-specialized** model trained on 5.5T code-focused tokens with reported HumanEval ~70.7 and MBPP ~69.2 (instruct/chat evaluation).
- **Qwen3-1.7B** is a **general-purpose** model, not code-specialized. Its base model EvalPlus is 52.70 (avg of HumanEval, MBPP, HumanEval+, MBPP+).
- The post-trained Qwen3-1.7B (instruct) with **thinking mode enabled** likely scores significantly higher on coding tasks due to chain-of-thought reasoning, potentially approaching or exceeding Qwen2.5-Coder-1.5B on simpler coding benchmarks.
- For **pure code completion** tasks, Qwen2.5-Coder-1.5B likely still wins due to code-specific training (FIM support, repo-level training). For **reasoning about code** and general coding chat, Qwen3-1.7B with thinking mode is likely superior.

---

## 4. Quantizations & Model Sizes

### GGUF (Ollama/llama.cpp):
| Quant | Qwen3-1.7B Size | Source |
|---|---|---|
| **Q4_K_M** (default ollama) | **~1.4 GB** | ollama.com/library/qwen3:1.7b |
| Full BF16 | ~3.4 GB | Estimated (1.7B Ă 2 bytes) |

Available via: `ollama run qwen3:1.7b` (default Q4_K_M)
Also: bartowski/Qwen_Qwen3-1.7B-GGUF, unsloth/Qwen3-1.7B-GGUF on HuggingFace (multiple quant levels including Q2, Q3, Q4, Q5, Q6, Q8)

### MLX (Apple Silicon):
From the **mlx-community** HuggingFace collection:

**Qwen3-1.7B MLX versions:**
| Model | Quant | Est. Size | Downloads |
|---|---|---|---|
| mlx-community/Qwen3-1.7B-bf16 | bf16 | ~3.4 GB | 64 |
| mlx-community/Qwen3-1.7B-8bit | 8-bit | ~1.7 GB | 130 |
| mlx-community/Qwen3-1.7B-6bit | 6-bit | ~1.3 GB | 64 |
| mlx-community/Qwen3-1.7B-4bit | **4-bit** | **~1.0 GB** | **19,300** (most popular) |
| mlx-community/Qwen3-1.7B-3bit | 3-bit | ~0.8 GB | 61 |

Also official Qwen MLX versions: `Qwen/Qwen3-1.7B-MLX-4bit`, `Qwen/Qwen3-1.7B-MLX-8bit`, `Qwen/Qwen3-1.7B-MLX-bf16`

**Qwen3-0.6B MLX versions:**
| Model | Quant | Est. Size | Downloads |
|---|---|---|---|
| mlx-community/Qwen3-0.6B-bf16 | bf16 | ~1.2 GB | 386 |
| mlx-community/Qwen3-0.6B-8bit | 8-bit | ~0.6 GB | 30,500 |
| mlx-community/Qwen3-0.6B-4bit | **4-bit** | **~0.4 GB** | **37,500** (most popular) |
| mlx-community/Qwen3-0.6B-6bit | 6-bit | ~0.5 GB | 118 |
| mlx-community/Qwen3-0.6B-3bit | 3-bit | ~0.3 GB | 74 |

### Other Quantization Formats:
- **GPTQ, AWQ** available via standard Qwen3 repos
- Qwen3 is noted as **"particularly quantization-friendly"** â even 2-bit versions show strong performance per research article on kaitchup.substack.com

---

## 5. Community Reviews & Opinions

**Positive:**
- Blog post (qwenlm.github.io): "Qwen3-1.7B/4B/8B/14B/32B-Base performs as well as Qwen2.5-3B/7B/14B/32B/72B-Base, respectively" â effectively 2x parameter efficiency
- Thinking mode is unique at this size â no other ~1.7B model offers hybrid reasoning
- Dev.to article: "The size to performance ratio with Qwen models is great" and "for chatting or writing code it's pretty nice"
- LM Studio user: Successfully used Qwen3-0.6B as a speculative decoding draft model for Qwen3-14B, getting 2-3x speed gains
- llm-explorer.com: Scored "LLM Explorer Score: 0.28" for the 4-bit version, lists VRAM ~1GB, Context ~40K

**Negative/Mixed:**
- Community user on Dev.to: "anything below 3B is mediocre at best" for complex tasks; 3B is the "transition point" for quality
- Another user: Compared to Gemini 2.5 Pro, Qwen3 (large models) reasoning described as "junior student" level
- At 1.7B, don't expect production-quality code generation â better suited for simple tasks, drafts, or speculative decoding

---

## 6. Summary Comparison Table

| Feature | Qwen3-1.7B | Qwen3-0.6B | Qwen2.5-Coder-1.5B |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Params** | 1.7B | 0.6B | 1.5B |
| **Type** | General (hybrid thinking) | General (hybrid thinking) | Code-specialized |
| **Context** | 32K | 32K | 128K |
| **EvalPlus (base)** | 52.70 | 36.23 | ~44.80 (Qwen2.5-1.5B-Base) |
| **MBPP (base)** | 55.40 | 36.60 | ~43.60 (Qwen2.5-1.5B-Base) |
| **HumanEval (instruct)** | N/A (est. higher w/ thinking) | N/A | ~70.7 (reported) |
| **Thinking mode** | â Yes | â Yes | â No |
| **FIM/Code completion** | â No | â No | â Yes |
| **Languages (NL)** | 119 | 119 | English-focused |
| **License** | Apache 2.0 | Apache 2.0 | Apache 2.0 |
| **4-bit size** | ~1.0-1.4 GB | ~0.4 GB | ~1.0 GB |

**Bottom line:** Qwen3-1.7B is a remarkably capable general-purpose model for its size, with coding benchmarks that significantly exceed Qwen2.5-1.5B (general) and approach Qwen2.5-Coder-1.5B territory, while also offering hybrid thinking mode, 119-language support, and tool-use capabilities. For pure code completion/FIM tasks, Qwen2.5-Coder-1.5B remains more specialized. For reasoning-about-code, agentic tasks, and multilingual use, Qwen3-1.7B is the clear winner.
